     <p><b>University at Buffalo, The State University of New York</b>, also commonly known as the <b>University at Buffalo</b> (abbreviated <b>UB</b>) or <b>SUNY Buffalo</b>, is a premier <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university" class="mw-redirect">research university</a> with multiple campuses located in <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">Buffalo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amherst,_New_York" title="Amherst, New York">Amherst</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York" title="New York">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. The university was founded in 1846 as a private college, but in 1962 was absorbed into the <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York" title="State University of New York">State University of New York</a> (SUNY) system. By enrollment, UB is the largest of SUNY's four comprehensive university centers,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> and also the largest public university in the northeastern United States (comprising New York state and the <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> region). In addition, by either endowment or research funding, UB is also the largest one of SUNY's four comprehensive flagship university centers.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the university enrolls 28,601 students<sup id="cite_ref-buffalo.edu_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buffalo.edu-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> in 13 separate colleges. The university houses the largest state-operated <a href="/wiki/Medical_school" title="Medical school">medical school</a> and features the only state <a href="/wiki/Law_school" title="Law school">law school</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">architecture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urban_planning" title="Urban planning">urban planning</a> school, and <a href="/wiki/Pharmacy" title="Pharmacy">pharmacy</a> school in the state of New York. The university offers over 100 bachelor's, 205 master's, 84 doctoral, and 10 professional areas of study.</p> 
     <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Classification_of_Institutions_of_Higher_Education" title="Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education">Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education</a>, the University at Buffalo is a Research University with Very High Research Activity (RU/VH). In 1989, UB was elected to the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>, which represents 62 prestigious, leading research universities in the United States and Canada. UB's alumni and faculty have produced a <a href="/wiki/U.S._President" title="U.S. President" class="mw-redirect">U.S. President</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Abdullahi_Farmajo" title="Mohamed Abdullahi Farmajo">Prime Minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Astronauts" title="Astronauts" class="mw-redirect">astronauts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_laureates" title="Nobel laureates" class="mw-redirect">Nobel laureates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners, <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Award</a> winners, <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholars" title="Rhodes Scholars" class="mw-redirect">Rhodes Scholars</a>, and other notable individuals in their fields.</p> 
     <p>Buffalo has consistently placed in the top cluster of U.S. public research universities and among the overall top 30 research universities according to the <i><a href="/wiki/Center_for_Measuring_University_Performance" title="Center for Measuring University Performance">Center for Measuring University Performance</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Center_for_Measuring_University_Performance_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Center_for_Measuring_University_Performance-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> and was ranked as the 38th best value for in-state students and the 27th best value for out of state students in the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Kiplinger" title="Kiplinger">Kiplinger</a> rankings of best value of national universities. <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report" class="mw-redirect">U.S. News and World Report</a></i><span style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s 2013 edition of America's Best Colleges ranked UB 106th on their list of &quot;Best National Universities,&quot; and 51st among public universities.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 2012-2013 edition of &quot;World University Rankings&quot;, <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a></i> ranked UB at 198, making it one of the top universities in the world.</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Millard_Fillmore_by_George_PA_Healy,_1857.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Millard_Fillmore_by_George_PA_Healy%2C_1857.jpg/170px-Millard_Fillmore_by_George_PA_Healy%2C_1857.jpg" width="170" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Millard_Fillmore_by_George_PA_Healy%2C_1857.jpg/255px-Millard_Fillmore_by_George_PA_Healy%2C_1857.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Millard_Fillmore_by_George_PA_Healy%2C_1857.jpg/340px-Millard_Fillmore_by_George_PA_Healy%2C_1857.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Millard_Fillmore_by_George_PA_Healy,_1857.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Official White House portrait of 
        <a href="/wiki/Millard_Fillmore" title="Millard Fillmore">Millard Fillmore</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>City leaders of Buffalo sought the establishment of a university in the city from the earliest days of Buffalo. A <b>University of Western New York</b> was begun at Buffalo under the auspices of the <a href="/wiki/United_Presbyterian_Church_in_the_United_States_of_America" title="United Presbyterian Church in the United States of America">Presbyterian Church</a> and property was purchased at North Street and College, (the site of the later YMCA), on the north side of the <a href="/wiki/Allentown,_Buffalo,_New_York" title="Allentown, Buffalo, New York">Allentown district</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hough_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hough-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> This university was chartered by the state on April 8, 1836. However, the project collapsed and no classes were ever offered, and only the layout of College Street remains.<sup id="cite_ref-Hough_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hough-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <b>University of Buffalo</b> was founded on May 11, 1846<sup id="cite_ref-Hough_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hough-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> as a private medical school to train the doctors for the communities of <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">Buffalo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Falls,_New_York" title="Niagara Falls, New York">Niagara Falls</a>, and surrounding villages. James Platt White was instrumental in obtaining a charter for the University of Buffalo from the state legislature in 1846. He also taught the first class of 89 men in obstetrics. State Assemblyman <a href="/wiki/Nathan_K._Hall" title="Nathan K. Hall">Nathan K. Hall</a> was also &quot;particularly active in procuring the charter&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-Hough2_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hough2-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The doors first opened to students in 1847 and after associating with a hospital for teaching purposes, the first class of students graduated the medical school in July 1847. The first chancellor of the University was future President of the United States <a href="/wiki/Millard_Fillmore" title="Millard Fillmore">Millard Fillmore</a>. Upon his ascension to the presidency after President Taylor's death, Fillmore stayed on as part-time chancellor. Fillmore's name now graces the continuing education school Millard Fillmore College located on the South Campus as well as the Millard Fillmore Academic Center, an academic and administrative services building at the core of the residential Joseph Ellicott Complex, located on the North Campus.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Pub_Scene_Singing_Alma_Mater.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Pub_Scene_Singing_Alma_Mater.jpg/270px-Pub_Scene_Singing_Alma_Mater.jpg" width="270" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Pub_Scene_Singing_Alma_Mater.jpg/405px-Pub_Scene_Singing_Alma_Mater.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Pub_Scene_Singing_Alma_Mater.jpg/540px-Pub_Scene_Singing_Alma_Mater.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Pub_Scene_Singing_Alma_Mater.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Pub Scene, students singing
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>&quot;The first lectures were delivered in a wooden building over the old post office, corner of Seneca and Washington streets.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-Hough2_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hough2-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> The first building specially built for the university was a stone building at the corner of Main and Virginia streets, built in 1849-50, through donations, public subscription, and a state grant.<sup id="cite_ref-Hough2_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hough2-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>There were continuous expansions to the college medical programs, including a separate pharmacy division, which is now The School of Pharmacy and Pharmaceutical Sciences. In 1887 a law school was organized in Buffalo, which quickly became associated with <a href="/wiki/Niagara_University" title="Niagara University">Niagara University</a> just to the north of Buffalo. After four years, in 1891, the law school was acquired by the University of Buffalo as the <a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo_Law_School" title="University at Buffalo Law School">University of Buffalo Law School</a>, which had a downtown Buffalo facility.</p> 
     <p>In the first few years of the 20th century, the University began planning for a comprehensive undergraduate college to complete the basic structure of a university, and in 1909 the University acquired the Erie County Almshouse grounds from the county of Erie, which became the University of Buffalo's initial campus. The establishment may have been influenced by the 1910 <a href="/wiki/Flexner_Report" title="Flexner Report">Flexner Report</a> which criticized the preparation of the medical students at the university.<sup id="cite_ref-Why_Innovation_Fails_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Why_Innovation_Fails-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> With that additional space, in 1915, the then University of Buffalo formed the <a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo_College_of_Arts_%26_Sciences" title="University at Buffalo College of Arts &amp; Sciences" class="mw-redirect">College of Arts and Sciences</a>, creating an undergraduate division in addition to its prior educational work in the licensed professional fields. In 1916, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Grace_Millard_Knox&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Grace Millard Knox (page does not exist)">Grace Millard Knox</a> pledged $500,000 for the establishment of a &quot;department of liberal arts and sciences in the University of Buffalo,&quot; which was at the time still a private institution. The initial gift of $100,000 was for the purchase of what would become Townsend Hall and the remainder was to establish the university's first endowment, in her husband's name, to support the department.<sup id="cite_ref-A_History_of_the_University_of_Buffalo_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_History_of_the_University_of_Buffalo-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Early_university_at_buffalo_1900.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/83/Early_university_at_buffalo_1900.png/170px-Early_university_at_buffalo_1900.png" width="170" height="216" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/83/Early_university_at_buffalo_1900.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/83/Early_university_at_buffalo_1900.png 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Early_university_at_buffalo_1900.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> First home of the Medical College
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 1950, the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Engineering" title="Industrial Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Industrial Engineering</a> department branched off from the <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_Engineering" title="Mechanical Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Mechanical Engineering</a> department. In 1956, a <a href="/wiki/Civil_Engineering" title="Civil Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Civil Engineering</a> Department was formed under <a href="/wiki/Lehigh_University" title="Lehigh University">Lehigh University</a> graduate <a href="/wiki/Robert_L._Ketter" title="Robert L. Ketter">Robert L. Ketter</a>, who went on to become Dean of the <a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo%27s_School_of_Engineering_and_Applied_Sciences" title="University at Buffalo's School of Engineering and Applied Sciences">School of Engineering and Applied Sciences</a>, and later President of the University.</p> 
     <p>In 1959, <a href="/wiki/WBFO" title="WBFO">WBFO</a> was launched as an AM radio station by <a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo%27s_School_of_Engineering_and_Applied_Sciences" title="University at Buffalo's School of Engineering and Applied Sciences">UB's School of Engineering and Applied Sciences</a>, and run by UB's students. The station has since become the launching pad of two modern <a href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" title="National Public Radio" class="mw-redirect">National Public Radiopersonalities</a>: <a href="/wiki/Terri_Gross" title="Terri Gross" class="mw-redirect">Terri Gross</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ira_Flatow" title="Ira Flatow">Ira Flatow</a>.</p> 
     <p>In 1961, the Western New York nuclear research program was created. This program installed a miniature, active nuclear fission reactor on the University's South (Main Street) Campus. This program was not particularly active, nor could it compete with other government-run research labs, consequently, the programs performed in this facility were abandoned somewhat shortly after its inception. This reactor was formally decommissioned in 2005 with little fanfare due to material security concerns.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisition_by_the_SUNY_system_and_second_campus">Acquisition by the SUNY system and second campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Acquisition by the SUNY system and second campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In the early 1960s, the private University of Buffalo was purchased by and incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York" title="State University of New York">State University of New York</a> or SUNY system, and became known as the <b>State University of New York at Buffalo</b>, or SUNY at Buffalo, and more recently as the <b>University at Buffalo</b>. As a part of the agreement to merge the university into the SUNY system, the State began to build an extensive second campus for the university. In 1964, The State acquired several hundred acres in the town of <a href="/wiki/Amherst,_New_York" title="Amherst, New York">Amherst</a> on the northeast of Buffalo, for development as a comprehensive campus for the most non-medical disciplines at University at Buffalo. This is often called the North Campus, and the center of most University at Buffalo activities. The North Campus project included several major buildings, dormitory complexes, a separate spur of the Interstate highway, and a new lake. The undergraduate college, the law school, and graduate schools were all moved to the new campus.</p> 
     <p>During the late 1960s, the College of Arts and Sciences was divided into three separate schools: arts and letters, natural sciences and mathematics, and social sciences. During the 1998-1999 academic year, the three schools were reunited to re-create the existing College of Arts and Sciences., when the faculties of Arts &amp; Letters, Social Sciences, and Natural Sciences and Mathematics were combined, according to a memorandum issued by the <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York" title="State University of New York">State University of New York</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SUNY_memo_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SUNY_memo-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="UB_2020">UB 2020</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: UB 2020">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" style=""> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <td class="mbox-image"> 
         <div style="width: 52px;">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gnome_globe_current_event.svg" class="image"><img alt="Gnome globe current event.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Gnome_globe_current_event.svg/42px-Gnome_globe_current_event.svg.png" width="42" height="42" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Gnome_globe_current_event.svg/63px-Gnome_globe_current_event.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Gnome_globe_current_event.svg/84px-Gnome_globe_current_event.svg.png 2x" /></a>
         </div> </td> 
        <td class="mbox-text" style=""><span class="mbox-text-span">This article is <b>outdated</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small><i>(July 2012)</i></small> </span></td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>Started in 2004 under President John B. Simpson, UB 2020 is a <a href="/wiki/Strategic_planning" title="Strategic planning">strategic planning</a> initiative to develop and implement a vision for the university over the next 15 years.<sup id="cite_ref-overview_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> The centerpiece of UB 2020 is to add about 10,000 more students, 750 faculty members and 600 staff, increasing the size of the University by about 40 percent. UB 2020 also recognizes the university's contribution to the surrounding region. The most recent estimates of UB's impact on the local and regional economies of Western New York report approximately $1.7 billion are brought into the local economy from the presence of UB. This figure is also expected to rise by 40 percent, corresponding with UB’s institutional growth.</p> 
     <p>One of the keys to helping UB achieve the goals of the UB 2020 plan, proponents say, is the passage of S2020 and A2020 known as the UB 2020 Flexibility and Economic Growth Act, by the New York State Legislature. On June 3, 2009 the State Senate passed S2020 and sent the bill to the Assembly for their consideration.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The current president, <a href="/wiki/Satish_K._Tripathi" title="Satish K. Tripathi">Satish K. Tripathi</a>, has continued his vocal support of UB 2020<sup id="cite_ref-overview_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-overview_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template"><span title="&nbsp;since February 2013" style="white-space: nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot">dead link</a></i>]</span></sup> and has been actively engaging in campus-wide discussion on the proposed tuition increases introduced by the bill.<sup id="cite_ref-overview_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2011, the School of Medicine and Biomedical Sciences received an anonymous donation of $40 million from an alumnus who had graduated from the University during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WGRZ_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WGRZ-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> The donation will contribute to the $375 million project which will relocate the School of Medicine and Biomedical Sciences to UB's downtown campus.<sup id="cite_ref-UB_Reporter_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UB_Reporter-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> The new school will be designed by <a href="/wiki/HOK_Architects" title="HOK Architects" class="mw-redirect">HOK Architects</a>.</p> 
     <p>As of May 10th 2012, in a one-year-span, UB has spent $300m on the strategic plan to construct/open four new buildings including <a href="/wiki/Barbara_and_Jack_Davis_Hall" title="Barbara and Jack Davis Hall">Davis Hall</a>, William R. Greiner Residence Hall, Clinical and Translational Research Center and Kaleida Health medical research building.<sup id="cite_ref-Davis_Hall_Opening_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davis_Hall_Opening-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The university's official name is the &quot;University at Buffalo, The State University of New York&quot;, however also in common use is <i>University at Buffalo</i> which is seen as a less formal unofficial name, and simply <i>UB</i>. The university's athletic department, particularly on uniforms just use <i>Buffalo</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration_and_organization">Administration and organization</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Administration and organization">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Clark_Hall_on_UB%27s_South_Campus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Clark_Hall_on_UB%27s_South_Campus.jpg/220px-Clark_Hall_on_UB%27s_South_Campus.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Clark_Hall_on_UB%27s_South_Campus.jpg/330px-Clark_Hall_on_UB%27s_South_Campus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Clark_Hall_on_UB%27s_South_Campus.jpg/440px-Clark_Hall_on_UB%27s_South_Campus.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Clark_Hall_on_UB%27s_South_Campus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Clark Hall on UB's South Campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Buffalo is a public university and is one of four university centers of the 64 campuses in the <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York" title="State University of New York">State University of New York</a> (SUNY) which enrolled 467,845 students and employed 33,455 faculty in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-SUNY_Fast_Facts_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SUNY_Fast_Facts-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> SUNY is governed by a 17 member Board of Trustees, 15 of whom are appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_York" title="Governor of New York">Governor of New York</a> and the remaining two members being elected from the Student Assembly and University Faculty Senate. <a href="/wiki/Carl_McCall" title="Carl McCall">Carl McCall</a> is the Chairman of the SUNY Board of Trustees and <a href="/wiki/Nancy_L._Zimpher" title="Nancy L. Zimpher">Nancy L. Zimpher</a> is the Chancellor of the SUNY system. <a href="/wiki/Satish_K._Tripathi" title="Satish K. Tripathi">Satish K. Tripathi</a> was appointed by the SUNY Board of Trustees as the 15th president of the University at Buffalo in April 2011 after previously serving a six-year tenure as the UB provost and executive vice president for academic affairs. He receives compensation of $385,000, $115,000, and $150,000 annually from each of the university, SUNY Research Foundation, and the UB Foundation respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> The University at Buffalo Foundation (UB Foundation) was chartered in 1962 as an independent non-profit corporation and is controlled by a privately appointed board of trustees. It serves as a vehicle to raise private funds for the university, develop real estate, and manage endowment investments on behalf of the university.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> The foundation managed a $685.2 million endowment for FY2011.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UB is organized into 13 academic schools and colleges.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The <b>School of Architecture and Planning</b> is the only architecture school in the SUNY system and offers the only accredited professional masters degree in architecture. The School of Architecture and Planning awarded 96 baccalaureate degrees and 69 master's degrees.</li> 
      <li>The <b>College of Arts and Sciences</b> was founded in 1915 and is the largest and most comprehensive academic unit at UB with 25 academic departments, 12 academic programs, and 21 centers and institutes across the humanities, arts, and sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-General_Information_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-General_Information-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>The <b><a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York_at_Buffalo_School_of_Dental_Medicine" title="State University of New York at Buffalo School of Dental Medicine">School of Dental Medicine</a></b> was founded in 1892 and offers accredited programs in <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Dental_Surgery" title="Doctor of Dental Surgery" class="mw-redirect">DDS</a>, oral surgery, and other oral sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>The <b>Graduate School of Education</b> was founded in 1931 and is one of the largest graduate schools at UB. The school has four academic departments: counseling and educational psychology, educational leadership and policy, learning and instruction, and library and information science.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> In academic year 2008-2009, the Graduate School of Education awarded 472 master's degrees and 52 doctoral degrees.</li> 
      <li>The <b><a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo%27s_School_of_Engineering_and_Applied_Sciences" title="University at Buffalo's School of Engineering and Applied Sciences">School of Engineering and Applied Sciences</a></b> was founded in 1946 and offers undergraduate and graduate degrees in six departments. It is the largest public school of engineering in the state of New York.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>The <b><a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo_Law_School" title="University at Buffalo Law School">Law School</a></b> was founded in 1887 and is the only law school in the SUNY system.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> The school awarded 265 JD degrees in the 2009-2010 academic year.</li> 
      <li>The <b>School of Management</b> was founded in 1923 and offers <a href="/wiki/AACSB" title="AACSB" class="mw-redirect">AACSB</a>-accredited undergraduate, MBA, and doctoral degrees.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>The <b>School of Medicine and Biomedical Sciences</b> is the founding faculty of the UB and began in 1846. It offers undergraduate and graduate degrees in the biomedical and biotechnical sciences as well as a MD program and residencies.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>The <b>School of Nursing</b> was founded in 1936 and offers bachelors, masters, and doctoral degrees in nursing practice and patient care.</li> 
      <li>The <b>School of Pharmacy and Pharmaceutical Sciences</b> was founded in 1886, making it the second-oldest faculty at UB and the only pharmacy school in the SUNY system.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>The <b>School of Public Health and Health Professions</b> was founded in 2003 from the merger of the Department of Social and Preventive Medicine and the UB School of Health Related Professions. The school offers a bachelor's degree in exercise science as well as professional, master's and PhD degrees.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>The <b>School of Social Work</b> offers graduate <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Social_Work" title="Master of Social Work">MSW</a> and doctoral degrees in <a href="/wiki/Social_work" title="Social work">social work</a>.</li> 
      <li>The <b><a href="/wiki/Roswell_Park_Cancer_Institute" title="Roswell Park Cancer Institute">Roswell Park Cancer Institute</a> Graduate Division</b> was founded in 1898 by <a href="/wiki/Roswell_Park" title="Roswell Park" class="mw-redirect">Roswell Park</a> and is the oldest comprehensive cancer center in the world. It offers five PhD programs and a MS program in basic and translational biomedical research related to cancer.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Parker_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Parker_2.jpg/220px-Parker_2.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Parker_2.jpg/330px-Parker_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Parker_2.jpg/440px-Parker_2.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Parker_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Parker Hall, home to the School of Architecture and Planning
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>University at Buffalo is a large, public research university with very high research activity.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> The university has been accredited by the <a href="/wiki/Middle_States_Commission_on_Higher_Education" title="Middle States Commission on Higher Education" class="mw-redirect">Middle States Commission on Higher Education</a> since 1921.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2009, the university awarded 4,036 bachelors degrees across 74 undergraduate programs, 2,076 masters degree across 190 programs, 367 doctoral degrees across 83 programs, and 609 professional degrees across 18 programs.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The four-year, full-time undergraduate program comprises the majority of enrollments at the university which emphasizes a balanced curriculum across the arts, sciences, and professions.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> The university enrolled 18,493 undergraduate and 9,144 graduate students in the spring 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Enrollments_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Enrollments-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> Women make up 48% of the student body and 78% of the student body is from the state of <a href="/wiki/New_York" title="New York">New York</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UnivProfile_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UnivProfile-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> 7,204 students live on-campus, 10,172 students live off campus, and 11,505 students commute.<sup id="cite_ref-UnivProfile_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UnivProfile-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> Undergraduate tuition, room &amp; board, and fees for New York state residents for the 2011-2012 school year totals $18,681 and costs to out-of-state residents totals $27,461.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UB_health_%26_sciences_library_interior_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/UB_health_%26_sciences_library_interior_3.jpg/220px-UB_health_%26_sciences_library_interior_3.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/UB_health_%26_sciences_library_interior_3.jpg/330px-UB_health_%26_sciences_library_interior_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/UB_health_%26_sciences_library_interior_3.jpg/440px-UB_health_%26_sciences_library_interior_3.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UB_health_%26_sciences_library_interior_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> UB's Health and Sciences Library, Abbott Hall
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>UB's admission is selective with high levels of transfer-in as well as rolling admission deadlines.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> The university received 21,985 applications for the Class of 2015, admitted 11,298 (51.4%), and matriculated 3,154 (27.9%).<sup id="cite_ref-CDS_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Among first year students, 34% graduated in the top tenth of their high school class<sup id="cite_ref-Freshman_Admission_Criteria_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freshman_Admission_Criteria-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Interquartile_range" title="Interquartile range">interquartile range</a> was 500-610 for SAT reading, 550-650 for SAT math, and 23-28 on the ACT composite.<sup id="cite_ref-CDS_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> UB received 6,107 transfer applicants, admitted 3,623, and enrolled 1,850.</p> 
     <p>Emphasis has been placed on developing a community of research scientists centered around an economic initiative to promote Buffalo and create the Center of Excellence for Bioinformatics and Life Sciences as well as other advanced biomedical and engineering disciplines.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Total R&amp;D for the fiscal year of 2010 was at $349.6 million, ranking 61st, which is higher than that of <a href="/wiki/Brown_University" title="Brown University">Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_University" title="Dartmouth University">Dartmouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tufts_University" title="Tufts University">Tufts</a>, and others.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> UB offered an early <a href="/wiki/Computer_Science" title="Computer Science" class="mw-redirect">Computer Science</a> major (distinct from a mathematics major).<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, UB played a significant role as a crucial internet hub for the eastern seaboard during the internet's inception.</p> 
     <p>University at Buffalo academic and professional faculty are represented by United University Professions.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> The two UUP chapters at the University at Buffalo are Health Sciences and Buffalo Center. United University Professions has over 34,000 members at 29 campuses of SUNY.</p> 
     <p>The University at Buffalo is also one of only two public schools in New York to have a medical school and a dental school, the other being the <a href="/wiki/Stony_Brook_University" title="Stony Brook University">Stony Brook University</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions">Admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Admissions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>UB's admission is selective with high levels of transfer-in as well as rolling admission deadlines.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_36-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> The university received 21,985 applications for the Class of 2015, admitted 11,298 (51.4%), and matriculated 3,154 (27.9%).<sup id="cite_ref-CDS_43-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Among first year students, 35% graduated in the top tenth of their high school class<sup id="cite_ref-Freshman_Admission_Criteria_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freshman_Admission_Criteria-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Inter-quartile_range" title="Inter-quartile range" class="mw-redirect">inter-quartile range</a> was 500-610 for SAT reading, 550-650 for SAT math, and 24-29 on the ACT composite.<sup id="cite_ref-CDS_43-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> The class of 2014 included over 900 merit scholars and 320 honors college students. Within the honors college, the average combined math and reading SAT score was 1382, which was higher than the average SAT score of students admitted to <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">University of California, Berkeley</a>, and high school grade average for the incoming class was 97%.<sup id="cite_ref-Admissions_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Admissions-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> UB received 6,107 transfer applicants, admitted 3,623, and enrolled 1,850.</p>

     <p><br /> In the 2012-2013 edition of &quot;World University Rankings&quot;, <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a> ranked UB at 198. In <a href="/wiki/Kiplinger" title="Kiplinger">Kiplinger</a>'s &quot;Best Values in Public Colleges&quot; of 2012, the University at Buffalo ranks 38th in the nation for in-state students and 27th in the nation for out of state students.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Fosterhall2_UB_South.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Fosterhall2_UB_South.JPG/220px-Fosterhall2_UB_South.JPG" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Fosterhall2_UB_South.JPG/330px-Fosterhall2_UB_South.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Fosterhall2_UB_South.JPG/440px-Fosterhall2_UB_South.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Fosterhall2_UB_South.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Historic Foster Hall on UB's South Campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report" class="mw-redirect">U.S. News and World Report</a></i><span style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s 2013 edition of America's Best Colleges ranked UB 106th on their list of &quot;Best National Universities&quot;, and 51st among public universities. The <a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo%27s_School_of_Engineering_and_Applied_Sciences" title="University at Buffalo's School of Engineering and Applied Sciences">School of Engineering and Applied Sciences</a> is ranked 54th, the Law School is ranked 82nd, the School of Pharmacy and Pharmaceutical Sciences is ranked 17th, the School of Social Work is ranked 26th, and the School of Medicine and Biological Sciences is ranked 57th for best research.<sup id="cite_ref-US_News_Rankings_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_News_Rankings-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the School of Arts and Sciences, the economics department is ranked 79th, audiology is ranked 17th, English is ranked 41st, library and information studies is ranked 36th, math is 68th, physics is 85th, fine arts is 72nd, political science is 78th,history is 85th, physical therapy is 51st, computer science is 61st, chemistry is 74th, statistics is 62nd, and psychology is ranked 64th.<sup id="cite_ref-US_News_Rankings_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_News_Rankings-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The School of Management at UB is ranked 89th by U.S. News, 48th by <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> and 57th by <a href="/wiki/BusinessWeek" title="BusinessWeek" class="mw-redirect">BusinessWeek</a> for full-time MBA.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> The School of Education at UB is well regarded, and is 92nd, the School of Public Health and Health Professions is ranked 36th, the School of Nursing is ranked 79th with the anesthesia program ranking 17th.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo_Libraries" title="University at Buffalo Libraries">University at Buffalo Libraries</a>
     </div> 
     <p>UB has nine libraries on its North (Amherst), South (Buffalo), and Downtown (Buffalo) campuses. The libraries' 3.8 million-plus print volumes are augmented by extensive digital resources, including full-text electronic journals, databases, media, and special collections, which include the world's single largest collection of James Joyce manuscripts and artifacts.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campuses">Campuses</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Campuses">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The University at Buffalo is the state’s largest and most comprehensive<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>public university and is spread across three campuses: North Campus, South Campus, and Downtown Campus.<sup id="cite_ref-aboutcampus_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aboutcampus-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> The Sustainable Endowments Institute's College Sustainability Report Card awarded the university a B-.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Campus">North Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: North Campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The North Campus, a <a href="/wiki/Census-designated_place" title="Census-designated place">census-designated place</a> also called &quot;University at Buffalo&quot;, located in the suburb of <a href="/wiki/Amherst,_New_York" title="Amherst, New York">Amherst</a>, began in the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-Haar_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haar-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> Many academic programs, including the entirety of the undergraduate College of Arts and Sciences, the <a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo_Law_School" title="University at Buffalo Law School">University at Buffalo Law School</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo%27s_School_of_Engineering_and_Applied_Sciences" title="University at Buffalo's School of Engineering and Applied Sciences">School of Engineering and Applied Sciences</a>, the School of Management, the School of Pharmacy and Pharmaceutical Sciences, the Graduate School of Social Work, and the Graduate School of Education, as well as <a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo_Libraries#Lockwood_Memorial_Library" title="University at Buffalo Libraries">Lockwood Memorial Library</a>, Capen Library, and many administrative offices, are located on UB's North Campus.</p> 
     <p>The North Campus is home to administrative and academic offices. The main buildings are arranged along one academic &quot;spine&quot;, a second floor connecting corridor, that connects most of the main academic buildings. The whole campus covers 1,192 acres (5&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>) with 146 buildings containing 6,715,492 sq&nbsp;ft (623,890&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>), 10 residence halls and 5 apartment complexes.<sup id="cite_ref-aboutcampus_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aboutcampus-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> Its immense size also necessitated the creation of a shuttle system circling the academic sector and surrounding areas including the administrative complex, located nearly a quarter mile from the central academic area. When originally built by the state of New York, the North Campus was provided with two Interstate exits, from <a href="/wiki/Interstate_290_(New_York)" title="Interstate 290 (New York)">I-290</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interstate_990_(New_York)" title="Interstate 990 (New York)" class="mw-redirect">I-990</a>, its own internal parkway, the John James Audubon Parkway, and two small lakes created from <a href="/wiki/Ellicott_Creek" title="Ellicott Creek">Ellicott Creek</a>. As a census-designated place, the residential population recorded at the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 census</a> was 6,066.<sup id="cite_ref-Census_2010_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_2010-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The North Campus offers a variety of entertainment programming and activity for students. It contains the Student Union, which houses offices for the Student Association and student-interest clubs; Slee Hall, which presents contemporary and classical music concerts; <a href="/wiki/Alumni_Arena_(University_at_Buffalo)" title="Alumni Arena (University at Buffalo)">Alumni Arena</a>, the home-court for University Athletics; the <a href="/wiki/UB_Center_for_the_Arts" title="UB Center for the Arts">UB Center for the Arts</a>, a non-profit presenter of a wide variety of professional entertainment and <a href="/wiki/UB_Stadium" title="UB Stadium" class="mw-redirect">UB Stadium</a>, the 30,000 seat <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">Football</a> Stadium.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Campus">South Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: South Campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UBsouth_campus_wide_shot.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/UBsouth_campus_wide_shot.jpg/220px-UBsouth_campus_wide_shot.jpg" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/UBsouth_campus_wide_shot.jpg/330px-UBsouth_campus_wide_shot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/UBsouth_campus_wide_shot.jpg/440px-UBsouth_campus_wide_shot.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UBsouth_campus_wide_shot.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Overlooking UB's South Campus from Abbott Hall
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The South Campus, also known as the Main Street campus, located on 154 acres (0.62&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>) in North Buffalo, is the former grounds of the Erie County Almshouse and Insane Asylum, of which four buildings still remain (Hayes Hall, the former insane asylum; Wende Hall, a former maternity hospital; Hayes D; and Townsend Hall, a former nurses' quarters).<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> The college was designed by architect E.B. Green in 1910, and was intended to resemble <a href="/wiki/Trinity_College,_Dublin" title="Trinity College, Dublin">Trinity College, Dublin</a>. Its 53 buildings contain (3,045,198 sq&nbsp;ft (282,908&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>)) and include six resident halls.<sup id="cite_ref-aboutcampus_68-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aboutcampus-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> This campus is served by the northernmost <a href="/wiki/University_(Metro_Rail)" title="University (Metro Rail)">subway station</a> on Buffalo's Niagara Frontier <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Metro_Rail" title="Buffalo Metro Rail">Metro Rail</a> system.</p> 
     <p>Today, the South Campus is home to the School of Pharmacy and the School of Architecture and Urban Planning. The Medical School is currently in the process of moving from South Campus to the new Downtown Campus in Buffalo. In addition, the University at Buffalo South Campus is the home of the <a href="/wiki/WBFO" title="WBFO">WBFO</a> radio station, the University's biomedical science research complex, the <a href="/wiki/University_at_Buffalo_Libraries#Health_Sciences_Library" title="University at Buffalo Libraries">Health Sciences Library</a> and certain administrative offices. Additionally, 20 percent of UB's resident population continues to live in the original residential complexes located on the South (Main Street) Campus.</p> 
     <p>Adjacent to the UB South Campus is the UB Anderson Art Gallery,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> a converted elementary school with an all-glass atrium exhibit space.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Downtown_Campus">Downtown Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Downtown Campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In 2002, UB commissioned Boston firm Chan Krieger to create a third campus center.<sup id="cite_ref-Haar_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haar-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> The Downtown Campus is the site of UB's New York State Center of Excellence in Bioinformatics and Life Science, which partners in research with UB's Ira G. Ross Eye Institute<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Roswell_Park_Cancer_Institute" title="Roswell Park Cancer Institute">Roswell Park Cancer Institute</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hauptman-Woodward_Medical_Research_Institute" title="Hauptman-Woodward Medical Research Institute">Hauptman-Woodward Medical Research Institute</a> to compose the Buffalo-Niagara Medical Campus. Also located in the downtown area is UB's Research Institute on Addictions (RIA), Educational Opportunity Center (EOC)<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> and the Jacobs Executive Development Center (JEDC). The campus includes six major properties and a total of 43 buildings, counting shared lease space (588,506 sq&nbsp;ft (54,674&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>)).<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In September 2007, UB added the former <a href="/wiki/M._Wile_and_Company_Factory_Building" title="M. Wile and Company Factory Building">M. Wile and Company Factory Building</a> on the southeast corner of Goodell and Ellicott streets and the former <a href="/wiki/Trico_Plant_No._1" title="Trico Plant No. 1">Trico Products Corp. building complex</a> on the northwest corner of Goodell and Ellicott streets to its properties downtown. The UB Regional Institute, Center on Rehabilitation Synergy, and a number of pre-K-16 initiatives related to UB's civic engagement mission, such as the UB-Buffalo Public Schools Partnership office, are set to relocate to the first site. The latter location has been purchased to house additional biomedical- and life science-related businesses connected to the Buffalo-Niagara Medical Campus.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Teaching_hospitals">Teaching hospitals</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Teaching hospitals">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>UB's teaching hospitals include Buffalo General Hospital, the Erie County Medical Center (ECMC), Millard Fillmore Hospital, Roswell Park Cancer Institute and Veterans Affairs Western New York Health Care System. Additional facilities include free clinics such as the Kaleida Health's Niagara Family Health Center and the Lighthouse Free Medical Clinic, a program run by UB medical students.</p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Comprehensive_Physical_Plan">Comprehensive Physical Plan</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Comprehensive Physical Plan">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>The University at Buffalo has accumulated over 29,000 undergraduate and <a href="/wiki/Postgraduate_education" title="Postgraduate education">graduate students</a>, as well as 14,000 employees, across three campuses in the last 160 years. In order to accommodate both students and faculty, the university is currently implementing a $4.5 million Comprehensive Physical Plan to help in growth as well as to best utilize and enhance current facilities. Connecting all three campuses, as well as the facilities UB uses, is also a major element of the project. The firm granted the contract to lead the project is<a href="/wiki/Beyer_Blinder_Belle" title="Beyer Blinder Belle">Beyer Blinder Belle</a>.</p> 
     <p>The comprehensive physical planning process is broken into four phases. Currently, UB is implementing &quot;phase one&quot; by seeking input from the local and university communities to pinpoint issues, opportunities, and concerns related to this expansion. The project recognizes UB’s potential for excellence, in regard to the university's physical environment, by highlighting and evaluating various positive and negative attributes of the three campuses, including housing, circulation, functionality, landscape, and community interface.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
