     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Associations_and_activities">Associations and activities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Associations and activities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:112px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Crest_and_Logo_of_Bisonhead.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Crest_and_Logo_of_Bisonhead.png/110px-Crest_and_Logo_of_Bisonhead.png" width="110" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Crest_and_Logo_of_Bisonhead.png/165px-Crest_and_Logo_of_Bisonhead.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Crest_and_Logo_of_Bisonhead.png/220px-Crest_and_Logo_of_Bisonhead.png 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Crest_and_Logo_of_Bisonhead.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Bisonhead is a coed 
        <a href="/wiki/Honor_society" title="Honor society">senior society</a> on campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>UB boasts two student-run periodicals: <i><a href="/wiki/The_Spectrum_(newspaper)" title="The Spectrum (newspaper)">The Spectrum</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Generation_Magazine" title="Generation Magazine">Generation</a></i> magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> Both publications are distributed on campus. <i>The Spectrum</i> is the only independent publication<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. <i>Generation</i> is funded by advertising and through Sub-Board I,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> the student services corporation. UB also has a student radio station, WRUB.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> WRUB broadcasts all UB home football games and select road games, as well as most UB men's and women's home basketball games. After the retirement of <a href="/wiki/John_B._Simpson" title="John B. Simpson">John B. Simpson</a>, the undergraduate students have also developed a university forum<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> with the hopes of developing a thriving online campus. This move was supported by now incumbent president <a href="/wiki/Satish_K_Tripathi" title="Satish K Tripathi" class="mw-redirect">Satish K Tripathi</a> who called it a &quot;model of University spirit and entrepreneurship&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1923, an honorary senior society called Bisonhead was founded. It has since represented twelve undergraduate leaders at UB each year.<sup id="cite_ref-Spectrum_article_on_Bisonhead_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spectrum_article_on_Bisonhead-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UB annually hosts the world’s largest mud-volleyball game known as “Ooz-fest”. Teams of at least six students compete in a double elimination volleyball tournament at “The Mud Pit” each April. Fire trucks are brought in to saturate the dirt courts to create the mud. Awards are handed out to not only the victors, but the most creatively dressed. In the past, students have worn business suits and even dresses to the tournament.</p> 
     <p>Many of UB clubs are run through the Undergraduate Student Association and the Graduate Student Association, with each level requiring respective senate recognition for clubs.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_housing">Student housing</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Student housing">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Student residence halls are located on both the North and South Campuses. On the North Campus, there is the Ellicott Complex, which consists of Fargo, Porter, Red Jacket, Richmond, Spaulding, and Wilkeson Quadrangles. Next to Fargo Quad is the newly built in 2011 Greiner Hall, a dorm strictly for sophomores. Also on North Campus is the Governors Complex, home to the Freshman Honors Housing and various other living communities. On South Campus is Goodyear and Clement Hall. The unique aspect of these dorms is that residents share a bathroom with the adjacent room, rather than have a communal bathroom. Up until Spring of 2011, there were three other dorm buildings, referred to as &quot;The Quad&quot;: MacDonald, Pritchard, Schoellkopf, and Michael Hall. Michael Hall currently exists as the Student Health Center, whereas the other three are closed and abandoned.</p> 
     <p>In 1999, the university built its first apartment complex for families and graduate students at Flickinger Court. Since the success of Flickinger, UB has developed South Lake Village, Hadley Village, Flint Village, and Creekside Apartments. Most students who wish to still live on or near the North Campus but enjoy the lifestyle of apartment living take advantage of these apartments. University Village at Sweethome and Villas at Chestnut Ridge are both student apartment communities adjacent to the North Campus and offer a shuttle service.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> Collegiate Village off campus apartments offers transportation to both North and South Campus.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> Students also find housing in private locations. Those locations are generally situated in the University Heights district of Buffalo, and other areas close to the North and South Campuses. The school assigns rooms based on a lottery system.</p> 
     <p><br /></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bulls" title="Buffalo Bulls">Buffalo Bulls</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The school's sports teams are known as the <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bulls" title="Buffalo Bulls">Buffalo Bulls</a>. However, the women's teams were originally called the Buffalo Royals.</p> 
     <p>In 1958, the football team won the <a href="/wiki/Lambert_Cup" title="Lambert Cup" class="mw-redirect">Lambert Cup</a>, emblematic of supremacy in Eastern U.S. small-college football. That led to the team's first bowl invitation, to the <a href="/wiki/Capital_One_Bowl" title="Capital One Bowl">Tangerine Bowl</a> in <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando, Florida</a>, against <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_University" title="Florida State University">Florida State University</a>. But the Bulls would be allowed to participate only if backup defensive end Mike Wilson and starting halfback <a href="/wiki/Willie_R._Evans_(running_back)" title="Willie R. Evans (running back)" class="mw-redirect">Willie Evans</a>, who were black, did not play. The team stood behind the two, and refused the bowl offer; Buffalo did not receive another bowl invitation until the 2008 season when they won the <a href="/wiki/Mid-American_Conference" title="Mid-American Conference">MAC</a> championship against previously undefeated <a href="/wiki/Ball_State_University" title="Ball State University">Ball State</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Several UB football stars from the 1950s and early 1960s went on to play professional football, including quarterback <a href="/wiki/John_Stofa" title="John Stofa">John Stofa</a> with the <a href="/wiki/American_Football_League" title="American Football League">American Football League</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Miami_Dolphins" title="Miami Dolphins">Miami Dolphins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Bengals" title="Cincinnati Bengals">Cincinnati Bengals</a>, and defensive lineman <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Philbin" title="Gerry Philbin">Gerry Philbin</a> with the <a href="/wiki/American_Football_League" title="American Football League">AFL</a>'s <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">New York Jets</a>. Philbin is a member of the AFL Hall of Fame and the <a href="/wiki/All-time_All-AFL_Team" title="All-time All-AFL Team" class="mw-redirect">All-time All-AFL Team</a>. Philbin and UB's <a href="/w/index.php?title=Willie_Ross_(American_football)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Willie Ross (American football) (page does not exist)">Willie Ross</a> were the first two UB graduates to play on professional football championship teams in the United States: Ross with the 1964 AFL Champion <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bills" title="Buffalo Bills">Buffalo Bills</a>; and Philbin with the 1968 AFL Champion <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">New York Jets</a>, who also won that season's <a href="/wiki/Professional_American_football_championship_games" title="Professional American football championship games">AFL-NFL World Championship Game</a> (Super Bowl III). <a href="/wiki/James_Starks" title="James Starks">James Starks</a> was on the Green Bay Packers Super Bowl XLV champions as a rookie. <a href="/wiki/Ramon_Guzman" title="Ramon Guzman">Ramon Guzman</a> played on the 2009 <a href="/wiki/Grey_Cup" title="Grey Cup">Grey Cup</a> champion <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Alouettes" title="Montreal Alouettes">Montreal Alouettes</a>.</p> 
     <p>Since 1996, the UB teams have participated in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a>'s Division I (I-A for <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a>), in the <a href="/wiki/Mid-American_Conference" title="Mid-American Conference">Mid-American Conference</a>. The mascots are 'Victor E. Bull', a blue bull with a gold nose ring, and his sister 'Victoria S. Bull'. After several years of poor performance in the two most popular college sports, men's basketball and football, the university's men's basketball team has recently begun to show some promise. In March 2005, the men's basketball team reached the Mid-American Conference Championship game, but suffered a harrowing 79-80 loss to the Ohio Bobcats, thus missing a chance for their first trip to the NCAA Tournament.</p> 
     <p>On March 25, 2009, the athletic department announced that the rowing program has joined the <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Athletic_Association" title="Colonial Athletic Association">Colonial Athletic Association</a> as an associate member. The Women's Rowing team went on to win the CAA championship in April 2010 for the first time. In May 2010, the team won the Jack &amp; Nancy Seitz Women's Point Trophy at the Dad Vail Regatta for the third year in a row, nicknamed the &quot;threepeat&quot; by Head Coach Rudy Wieler.</p> 
     <p>With the hiring of <a href="/wiki/Turner_Gill" title="Turner Gill">Turner Gill</a> as head football coach in 2006, UB was the only Division I-A school with an African American athletic director (Warde Manuel), men's basketball head coach (Reggie Witherspoon), and football head coach (Gill).</p> 
     <p>The university is home to the <a href="/wiki/Thunder_of_the_East" title="Thunder of the East" class="mw-redirect">Thunder of the East</a> marching band. The band performs at all home football games and travels to both local and national parades and competitions.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Jamey_Richard" title="Jamey Richard">Jamey Richard</a>, a 2008 graduate, plays in the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> and was selected by the <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis_Colts" title="Indianapolis Colts">Indianapolis Colts</a> in the 7th round, with the 236 pick of the <a href="/wiki/2008_NFL_Draft" title="2008 NFL Draft">2008 NFL Draft</a>. <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Scott" title="Trevor Scott">Trevor Scott</a>, 2008 graduate of the University of Buffalo, plays in the NFL and was selected by the <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Raiders" title="Oakland Raiders">Oakland Raiders</a>. Quarterback <a href="/wiki/Drew_Willy" title="Drew Willy">Drew Willy</a>, 2009 graduate of the University of Buffalo, originally signed with the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Ravens" title="Baltimore Ravens">Baltimore Ravens</a> and later the practice squad of the <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis_Colts" title="Indianapolis Colts">Indianapolis Colts</a>. He was on the active roster for the Colts for one game and was with the team for Super Bowl XLIV. He is currently on the roster of the New York Jets. James Starks (6th round, 193rd overall) now plays with the <a href="/wiki/Green_Bay_Packers" title="Green Bay Packers">Green Bay Packers</a>. And Naaman Roosevelt (Undrafted, started off as a player on the practice squad, but moved to the big club later on) who plays for the <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bills" title="Buffalo Bills">Buffalo Bills</a><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Buffalo has three fight songs: &quot;Victory March&quot;, &quot;Go For a Touchdown&quot;, and &quot;Buffalo Fight Song&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_faculty_and_alumni">Notable faculty and alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Notable faculty and alumni">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_at_Buffalo_people" title="List of University at Buffalo people">List of University at Buffalo people</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Among the individuals who have attended, graduated, and taught at the University are astronaut <a href="/wiki/Ellen_S._Baker" title="Ellen S. Baker">Ellen S. Baker</a>, American journalist <a href="/wiki/Wolf_Blitzer" title="Wolf Blitzer">Wolf Blitzer</a>, CEO and founder of the History Channel <a href="/wiki/Abbe_Raven" title="Abbe Raven" class="mw-redirect">Abbe Raven</a>, CEO of Paramount Pictures <a href="/wiki/Brad_Grey" title="Brad Grey">Brad Grey</a>, billionaire and CEO of Baidu <a href="/wiki/Robin_Li" title="Robin Li">Robin Li</a>, Pulitzer Prize-winner <a href="/wiki/Tom_Toles" title="Tom Toles">Tom Toles</a>, Nobel Prize-winners, <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Coase" title="Ronald Coase">Ronald Coase</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herbert_A._Hauptman" title="Herbert A. Hauptman">Herbert A. Hauptman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sir_John_Carew_Eccles" title="Sir John Carew Eccles" class="mw-redirect">Sir John Carew Eccles</a>, and winners of the <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Technology_and_Innovation" title="National Medal of Technology and Innovation">National Medal of Technology and Innovation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norman_McCombs" title="Norman McCombs">Norman McCombs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wilson_Greatbach" title="Wilson Greatbach" class="mw-redirect">Wilson Greatbach</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Erich_Bloch" title="Erich Bloch">Erich Bloch</a>. Billionaire and owner of the Boston Bruins, <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Jacobs" title="Jeremy Jacobs">Jeremy Jacobs</a>, musician and civil rights activist <a href="/wiki/Charles_Mingus" title="Charles Mingus">Charles Mingus</a>, civil engineer, genealogist and author <a href="/wiki/Angelo_F._Coniglio" title="Angelo F. Coniglio">Angelo F. Coniglio</a>, and American actor, director, and producer <a href="/wiki/Ron_Silver" title="Ron Silver">Ron Silver</a>. Amongst the athletes who have graduated from the University are football players <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Philbin" title="Gerry Philbin">Gerry Philbin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naaman_Roosevelt" title="Naaman Roosevelt">Naaman Roosevelt</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Starks" title="James Starks">James Starks</a> along with soccer players, <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Shuttleworth" title="Bobby Shuttleworth">Bobby Shuttleworth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martin_John" title="Martin John">Martin John</a>.</p> 
     <p>Over the years the University at Buffalo has also been particularly distinguished in contemporary creative writing. Noted novelists who have taught on its faculty include <a href="/wiki/John_Barth" title="John Barth">John Barth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Federman" title="Raymond Federman">Raymond Federman</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Burgess" title="Anthony Burgess">Anthony Burgess</a>. Noted faculty poets include George Starbuck (1983 <a href="/wiki/Lenore_Marshall_Poetry_Prize" title="Lenore Marshall Poetry Prize" class="mw-redirect">Lenore Marshall Prize</a>), <a href="/wiki/Charles_Olson" title="Charles Olson">Charles Olson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Creeley" title="Robert Creeley">Robert Creeley</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bollingen_Prize" title="Bollingen Prize">Bollingen Prize</a> 1999), <a href="/wiki/John_Logan_(poet)" title="John Logan (poet)">John Logan</a>, (<a href="/wiki/Lenore_Marshall_Poetry_Prize" title="Lenore Marshall Poetry Prize" class="mw-redirect">Lenore Marshall Prize</a> 1982), <a href="/wiki/Irving_Feldman" title="Irving Feldman">Irving Feldman</a> (<a href="/wiki/MacArthur_Foundation_Fellowship" title="MacArthur Foundation Fellowship" class="mw-redirect">MacArthur Foundation Fellow</a> 1992), <a href="/wiki/Carl_Dennis" title="Carl Dennis">Carl Dennis</a> (2000 <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Lilly_Poetry_Prize" title="Ruth Lilly Poetry Prize">Ruth Lilly Poetry Prize</a>; 2002 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize_for_Poetry" title="Pulitzer Prize for Poetry">Pulitzer Prize for Poetry</a>), <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hass" title="Robert Hass">Robert Hass</a> (<a href="/wiki/Poet_Laureate_of_the_United_States" title="Poet Laureate of the United States" class="mw-redirect">Poet Laureate of the United States</a> 1995-97, 2007 <a href="/wiki/National_Book_Award" title="National Book Award">National Book Award</a>, 2008 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize_for_Poetry" title="Pulitzer Prize for Poetry">Pulitzer Prize for Poetry</a>), <a href="/wiki/Charles_Bernstein" title="Charles Bernstein">Charles Bernstein</a> (co-founder of the University's notable Poetics Program), <a href="/wiki/Steve_McCaffery" title="Steve McCaffery">Steve McCaffery</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Susan_Howe" title="Susan Howe">Susan Howe</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bollingen_Prize" title="Bollingen Prize">Bollingen Prize</a> 2011). Former UB students include Michael Casey (<a href="/wiki/Yale_Younger_Poets_Award" title="Yale Younger Poets Award" class="mw-redirect">Yale Younger Poets Award</a>), <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Petrosky" title="Anthony Petrosky">Tony Petrosky</a> (<a href="/wiki/Walt_Whitman_Award" title="Walt Whitman Award" class="mw-redirect">Walt Whitman Award</a>), <a href="/wiki/Donald_Revell" title="Donald Revell">Donald Revell</a> (2004 <a href="/wiki/Lenore_Marshall_Poetry_Prize" title="Lenore Marshall Poetry Prize" class="mw-redirect">Lenore Marshall Prize</a>), <a href="/wiki/Charles_Baxter_(author)" title="Charles Baxter (author)">Charles Baxter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Willis" title="Elizabeth Willis">Elizabeth Willis</a>.</p> 
     <p>Political leaders that have attended and taught at the University, include the 13th President of the United States, <a href="/wiki/Millard_Fillmore" title="Millard Fillmore">Millard Fillmore</a>, Prime Minister of Somalia, <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Abdullahi_Farmajo" title="Mohamed Abdullahi Farmajo">Mohamed Abdullahi Farmajo</a>, and the Minister of Education of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China" class="mw-redirect">People's Republic of China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zhou_Ji" title="Zhou Ji">Zhou Ji</a>.</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_at_Buffalo,_The_State_University_of_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: References">edit</a>]</span></h2>
